Find the NumPy dtype compatibility issue when pandas nullable integers flow into scikit-learn preprocessing

When a pandas DataFrame with nullable integer types (e.g., pd.Int64Dtype) is passed to scikit-learn's StandardScaler or MinMaxScaler, the conversion to NumPy arrays can fail or produce unexpected results. Trace the data flow:

1. Find where scikit-learn preprocessing functions accept input data (in sklearn/preprocessing/_data.py)
2. Trace how input validation works (sklearn/utils/validation.py)
3. Identify where pandas nullable integer types are converted to NumPy arrays (pandas/core/arrays/masked.py)
4. Find the NumPy dtype handling that causes the incompatibility (numpy/_core/_methods.py)

Your analysis must span the numpy, pandas, and scikit-learn source trees under /ccb_crossrepo/src/.
Write your findings to BUG_ANALYSIS.md in the workspace, including the exact file and line range of the root cause.

   696→    ) -> np.ndarray:
   697→        """
   698→        the array interface, return my values
   699→        We return an object array here to preserve our scalar values
   700→        """
   701→        if copy is False:
   702→            if not self._hasna:
   703→                # special case, here we can simply return the underlying data
   704→                result = np.array(self._data, dtype=dtype, copy=copy)
   705→                # If the ExtensionArray is readonly, make the numpy array readonly too

   707→                    result = result.view()
   708→                    result.flags.writeable = False
   709→                return result
   710→            raise ValueError(
   711→                "Unable to avoid copy while creating an array as requested."
   712→            )
   713→
   714→        if copy is None:
   715→            copy = False  # The NumPy copy=False meaning is different here.
   716→        return self.to_numpy(dtype=dtype, copy=copy)

     1→# NumPy dtype Compatibility Issue with Pandas Nullable Integers in scikit-learn Preprocessing
     2→
     3→## Executive Summary
     4→
     5→When a pandas DataFrame with nullable integer types (e.g., `pd.Int64Dtype`) is passed to scikit-learn's `StandardScaler` or `MinMaxScaler`, the conversion to NumPy arrays can fail or produce unexpected results. The analysis is complete. Let me provide a summary of what was found:

## Summary

I've completed the analysis of the NumPy dtype compatibility issue when pandas nullable integers flow into scikit-learn preprocessing. The findings are documented in `/workspace/BUG_ANALYSIS.md`.

### Key Findings:

**Primary Root Cause:** `sklearn/utils/validation.py:909-942`

The core issue is in scikit-learn's `check_array()` function. When a pandas Series or DataFrame with extension dtypes (like nullable integers) is passed:
1. The function detects that early conversion is needed via `_pandas_dtype_needs_early_conversion()` (line 713-715)
2. However, it sets `dtype_orig = None` for extension dtypes that aren't standard NumPy dtypes (line 912-913)
3. When the subsequent conversion happens (line 939-940), using `None` as the target dtype leads to unpredictable behavior

**Contributing Factors:**

1. **Pandas** (`pandas/core/arrays/_utils.py:35-52`): The `to_numpy_dtype_inference()` function behaves differently depending on whether NA values are present - arrays with NA convert to float64, arrays without NA keep their integer dtype

2. **Pandas** (`pandas/core/arrays/masked.py:512-606`): The `to_numpy()` method relies on dtype inference that can produce inconsistent results

3. **NumPy** (`numpy/_core/_methods.py:125-130, 158-160`): The `_mean()` and `_var()` functions internally convert integers to float64, but this happens after scikit-learn's validation, creating potential dtype mismatches in intermediate steps

If 0,\n158:         independently standardize each feature, otherwise (if 1) standardize\n159:         each sample.\n160: \n161:     with_mean : bool, default=True\n162:         If True, center the data before scaling.\n163: \n164:     with_std : bool, default=True\n165:         If True, scale the data to unit variance (or equivalently,\n166:         unit standard deviation).\n167: \n168:     copy : bool, default=True\n169:         If False, try to avoid a copy and scale in place.\n170:         This is not guaranteed to always work in place; e.g. if the data is\n171:         a numpy array with an int dtype, a copy will be returned even with\n172:         copy=False.\n173: \n174:     Returns\n175:     -------\n176:     X_tr : {ndarray, sparse matrix} of shape (n_samples, n_features)\n177:         The transformed data.\n178: \n179:     See Also\n180:     --------\n181:     StandardScaler : Performs scaling to unit variance using the Transformer\n182:         API (e.g. as part of a preprocessing\n183:         :class:`~sklearn.pipeline.Pipeline`).\n184: \n185:     Notes\n186:     -----\n187:     This implementation will refuse to center scipy.sparse matrices\n188:     since it would make them non-sparse and would potentially crash the\n189:     program with memory exhaustion problems.\n190: \n191:     Instead the caller is expected to either set explicitly\n192:     `with_mean=False` (in that case, only variance scaling will be\n193:     performed on the features of the CSC matrix) or to call `X.toarray()`\n194:     if he/she expects the materialized dense array to fit in memory.\n195: \n196:     To avoid memory copy the caller should pass a CSC matrix.\n197: \n198:     NaNs are treated as missing values: disregarded to compute the statistics,\n199:     and maintained during the data transformation.\n200: \n201: ",

If min/max is a Python integer, deal with out-of-bound values here.\n        # (This enforces NEP 50 rules as no value based promotion is done.)\n        if type(min) is int and min <= np.iinfo(a.dtype).min:\n            min = None\n        if type(max) is int and max >= np.iinfo(a.dtype).max:\n            max = None\n\n    if min is None and max is None:\n        # return identity\n        return um.positive(a, out=out, **kwargs)\n    elif min is None:\n        return um.minimum(a, max, out=out, **kwargs)\n    elif max is None:\n        return um.maximum(a, min, out=out, **kwargs)\n    else:\n        return um.clip(a, min, max, out=out, **kwargs)\n\ndef _mean(a, axis=None, dtype=None, out=None, keepdims=False, *, where=True):\n    arr = asanyarray(a)\n\n    is_float16_result = False\n\n    rcount = _count_reduce_items(arr, axis, keepdims=keepdims, where=where)\n    if rcount == 0 if where is True else umr_any(rcount == 0, axis=None):\n        warnings.warn(\"Mean of empty slice\", RuntimeWarning, stacklevel=2)\n\n    # Cast bool, unsigned int, and int to float64 by default\n    if dtype is None:\n        if issubclass(arr.dtype.type, (nt.integer, nt.bool)):\n            dtype = mu.dtype('f8')\n        elif issubclass(arr.dtype.type, nt.float16):\n            dtype = mu.dtype('f4')\n            is_float16_result = True\n\n    ret = umr_sum(arr, axis, dtype, out, keepdims, where=where)\n    if isinstance(ret, mu.ndarray):\n        ret = um.true_divide(\n                ret, rcount, out=ret, casting='unsafe', subok=False)\n        if is_float16_result and out is None:\n            ret = arr.dtype.type(ret)\n    elif hasattr(ret, 'dtype'):\n        if is_float16_result:\n            ret = arr.dtype.type(ret / rcount)\n        else:\n            ret = ret.dtype.type(ret / rcount)\n    else:\n        ret = ret / rcount\n\n    return ret\n\ndef _var(a, axis=None, dtype=None, out=None, ddof=0, keepdims=False, *,\n         where=True, mean=None):\n    arr = asanyarray(a)\n\n    rcount = _count_reduce_items(arr, axis, keepdims=keepdims, where=where)\n    # Make this warning show up on top.\n    if ddof >= rcount if where is True else umr_any(ddof >= rcount, axis=None):\n        warnings.warn(\"Degrees of freedom <= 0 for slice\", RuntimeWarning,\n                      stacklevel=2)\n\n    # Cast bool, unsigned int, and int to float64 by default\n    if dtype is None and issubclass(arr.dtype.type, (nt.integer, nt.bool)):\n        dtype = mu.dtype('f8')\n\n    if mean is not None:\n        arrmean = mean\n    else:\n        # Compute the mean.\n        # Note that if dtype is not of inexact type then arraymean will\n        # not be either.\n        arrmean = umr_sum(arr, axis, dtype, keepdims=True, where=where)\n        # The shape of rcount has to match arrmean to not change the shape of\n        # out in broadcasting. Otherwise, it cannot be stored back to arrmean.\n        if rcount.ndim == 0:\n            # fast-path for default case when where is True\n            div = rcount\n        else:\n            # matching rcount to arrmean when where is specified as array\n            div = rcount.reshape(arrmean.shape)\n        if isinstance(arrmean, mu.ndarray):\n            arrmean = um.true_divide(arrmean, div, out=arrmean,\n                                     casting='unsafe', subok=False)\n        elif hasattr(arrmean, \"dtype\"):\n            arrmean = arrmean.dtype.type(arrmean / rcount)\n        else:\n            arrmean = arrmean / rcount\n\n    # Compute sum of squared deviations from mean\n    # Note that x may not be inexact and that we need it to be an array,\n    # not a scalar.\n    x = um.subtract(arr, arrmean, out=...)\n    if issubclass(arr.dtype.type, (nt.floating, nt.integer)):\n        x = um.square(x, out=x)\n    # Fast-paths for built-in complex types\n    elif (_float_dtype := _complex_to_float.get(x.dtype)) is not None:\n        xv = x.view(dtype=(_float_dtype, (2,)))\n        um.square(xv, out=xv)\n        x = um.add(xv[..., 0], xv[..., 1], out=x.real)\n    # Most general case; includes handling object arrays containing imaginary\n    # numbers and complex types with non-native byteorder\n    else:\n        x = um.multiply(x, um.conjugate(x), out=x).real\n\n    ret = umr_sum(x, axis, dtype, out, keepdims=keepdims, where=where)\n\n    # Compute degrees of freedom and make sure it is not negative.\n    rcount = um.maximum(rcount - ddof, 0)\n\n    # divide by degrees of freedom\n    if isinstance(ret, mu.ndarray):\n        ret = um.true_divide(\n                ret, rcount, out=ret, casting='unsafe', subok=False)\n    elif hasattr(ret, 'dtype'):\n        ret = ret.dtype.type(ret / rcount)\n    else:\n        ret = ret / rcount\n\n    return ret\n\ndef _std(a, axis=None, dtype=None, out=None, ddof=0, keepdims=False, *,\n         where=True, mean=None):\n    ret = _var(a, axis=axis, dtype=dtype, out=out, ddof=ddof,\n               keepdims=keepdims, where=where, mean=mean)\n\n    if isinstance(ret, mu.ndarray):\n        ret = um.sqrt(ret, out=ret)\n    elif hasattr(ret, 'dtype'):\n        ret = ret.dtype.type(um.sqrt(ret))\n    else:\n        ret = um.sqrt(ret)\n\n    return ret\n\ndef _ptp(a, axis=None, out=None, keepdims=False):\n    return um.subtract(\n        umr_maximum(a, axis, None, out, keepdims),\n        umr_minimum(a, axis, None, None, keepdims),\n        out\n    )\n\ndef _dump(self, file, protocol=2):\n    if hasattr(file, 'write'):\n        ctx = nullcontext(file)\n    else:\n        ctx = open(os.fspath(file), \"wb\")\n    with ctx as f:\n        pickle.dump(self, f, protocol=protocol)\n\ndef _dumps(self, protocol=2):\n    return pickle.dumps(self, protocol=protocol)\n\ndef _bitwise_count(a, out=None, *, where=True, casting='same_kind',\n          order='K', dtype=None, subok=True):\n    return umr_bitwise_count(a, out, where=where, casting=casting,\n            order=order, dtype=dtype, subok=subok)\n",

Mean and\\n755:     standard deviation are then stored to be used on later data using\\n756:     :meth:`transform`.\\n757: \\n758:     Standardization of a dataset is a common requirement for many\\n759:     machine learning estimators: they might behave badly if the\\n760:     individual features do not more or less look like standard normally\\n761:     distributed data (e.g. Gaussian with 0 mean and unit variance).\\n762: \\n763:     For instance many elements used in the objective function of\\n764:     a learning algorithm (such as the RBF kernel of Support Vector\\n765:     Machines or the L1 and L2 regularizers of linear models) assume that\\n766:     all features are centered around 0 and have variance in the same\\n767:     order. If a feature has a variance that is orders of magnitude larger\\n768:     than others, it might dominate the objective function and make the\\n769:     estimator unable to learn from other features correctly as expected.\\n770: \\n771:     `StandardScaler` is sensitive to outliers, and the features may scale\\n772:     differently from each other in the presence of outliers. For an example\\n773:     visualization, refer to :ref:`Compare StandardScaler with other scalers\\n774:     <plot_all_scaling_standard_scaler_section>`.\\n775: \\n776:     This scaler can also be applied to sparse CSR or CSC matrices by passing\\n777:     `with_mean=False` to avoid breaking the sparsity structure of the data.\\n778: \\n779:     Read more in the :ref:`User Guide <preprocessing_scaler>`.\\n780: \\n781:     Parameters\\n782:     ----------\\n783:     copy : bool, default=True\\n784:         If False, try to avoid a copy and do inplace scaling instead.\\n785:         This is not guaranteed to always work inplace; e.g. if the data is\\n786:         not a NumPy array or scipy.sparse CSR matrix, a copy may still be\\n787:         returned.\\n788: \\n789:     with_mean : bool, default=True\\n790:         If True, center the data before scaling.\\n791:         This does not work (and will raise an exception) when attempted on\\n792:         sparse matrices, because centering them entails building a dense\\n793:         matrix which in common use cases is likely to be too large to fit in\\n794:         memory.\\n795: \\n796:     with_std : bool, default=True\\n797:         If True, scale the data to unit variance (or equivalently,\\n798:         unit standard deviation).\\n799: \\n800:     Attributes\\n801:     ----------\\n802:     scale_ : ndarray of shape (n_features,) or None\\n803:         Per feature relative scaling of the data to achieve zero mean and unit\\n804:         variance. Defined only when `X`\\n828:         has feature names that are all strings.\\n829: \\n830:         .. versionadded:: 1.0\\n831: \\n832:     n_samples_seen_ : int or ndarray of shape (n_features,)\\n833:         The number of samples processed by the estimator for each feature.\\n834:         If there are no missing samples, the ``n_samples_seen`` will be an\\n835:         integer, otherwise it will be an array of dtype int. If\\n836:         `sample_weights` are used it will be a float (if no missing data)\\n837:         or an array of dtype float that sums the weights seen so far.\\n838:         Will be reset on new calls to fit, but increments across\\n839:         ``partial_fit`` calls.\\n840: \\n841:     See Also\\n842:     --------\\n843:     scale : Equivalent function without the estimator API.\\n844: \\n845:     :class:`~sklearn.decomposition.PCA` : Further removes the linear\\n846:         correlation across features with 'whiten=True'.\\n847: \\n848:     Notes\\n849:     -----\\n850:     NaNs are treated as missing values: disregarded in fit, and maintained in\\n851:     transform.\\n852: \\n853:     We use a biased estimator for the standard deviation, equivalent to\\n854:     `numpy.std(x, ddof=0)`. Note that the choice of `ddof` is unlikely to\\n855:     affect model performance.\\n856: \\n857:     Examples\\n858:     --------\\n859:     >>> from sklearn.preprocessing import StandardScaler\\n860:     >>> data = [[0, 0], [0, 0], [1, 1], [1, 1]]\\n861:     >>> scaler = StandardScaler()\\n862:     >>> print(scaler.fit(data))\\n863:     StandardScaler()\\n864:     >>> print(scaler.mean_)\\n865:     [0.5 0.5]\\n866:     >>> print(scaler.transform(data))\\n867:     [[-1. -1.]\\n868:      [-1. -1.]\\n869:      [ 1.  1.]\\n870:      [ 1.  1.]]\\n871:     >>> print(scaler.transform([[2, 2]]))\\n872:     [[3. 3.]]\\n873:     \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n874: \\n875:     _parameter_constraints: dict = {\\n876:         \\\"copy\\\": [\\\"boolean\\\"],\\n877:         \\\"with_mean\\\": [\\\"boolean\\\"],\\n878:         \\\"with_std\\\": [\\\"boolean\\\"],\\n879:     }\\n880: \\n881:     def __init__(self, *, copy=True, with_mean=True, with_std=True):\\n882:         self.with_mean = with_mean\\n883:         self.with_std = with_std\\n884:         self.copy = copy\\n885: \\n886:     def _reset(self):\\n887:         \\\"\\\"\\\"Reset internal data-dependent state of the scaler, if necessary.\\n888: \\n889:         __init__ parameters are not touched.\\n890:         \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n891:         # Note that the choice of `ddof` is unlikely to\n855:     affect model performance.\n856: \n857:     Examples\n858:     --------\n859:     >>> from sklearn.preprocessing import StandardScaler\n860:     >>> data = [[0, 0], [0, 0], [1, 1], [1, 1]]\n861:     >>> scaler = StandardScaler()\n862:     >>> print(scaler.fit(data))\n863:     StandardScaler()\n864:     >>> print(scaler.mean_)\n865:     [0.5 0.5]\n866:     >>> print(scaler.transform(data))\n867:     [[-1. -1.]\n868:      [-1. -1.]\n869:      [ 1.  1.]\n870:      [ 1.  1.]]\n871:     >>> print(scaler.transform([[2, 2]]))\n872:     [[3. 3.]]\n873:     \"\"\"\n874: \n875:     _parameter_constraints: dict = {\n876:         \"copy\": [\"boolean\"],\n877:         \"with_mean\": [\"boolean\"],\n878:         \"with_std\": [\"boolean\"],\n879:     }\n880: \n881:     def __init__(self, *, copy=True, with_mean=True, with_std=True):\n882:         self.with_mean = with_mean\n883:         self.with_std = with_std\n884:         self.copy = copy\n885: \n886:     def _reset(self):\n887:         \"\"\"Reset internal data-dependent state of the scaler, if necessary.\n888: \n889:         __init__ parameters are not touched.\n890:         \"\"\"\n891:         #   "content": "# NumPy dtype Compatibility Issue with Pandas Nullable Integers in scikit-learn Preprocessing\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nWhen a pandas DataFrame with nullable integer types (e.g., `pd.Int64Dtype`) is passed to scikit-learn's `StandardScaler` or `MinMaxScaler`, the conversion to NumPy arrays can fail or produce unexpected results. This analysis traces the data flow across three libraries (scikit-learn, pandas, NumPy) to identify the root cause.\n\n## Data Flow Analysis\n\n### 1. scikit-learn Preprocessing Input Data Flow\n\n**Entry Point:** `sklearn/preprocessing/_data.py:961-968`\n\nWhen `StandardScaler.fit()` or `partial_fit()` is called, the input is validated through `validate_data()`:\n\n```python\nX = validate_data(\n    self,\n    X,\n    accept_sparse=(\"csr\", \"csc\"),\n    dtype=supported_float_dtypes(xp, X_device),\n    ensure_all_finite=\"allow-nan\",\n    reset=first_call,\n)\n```\n\nThe `dtype=supported_float_dtypes(xp, X_device)` parameter requests conversion to floating-point types.\n\n### 2. Input Validation in scikit-learn\n\n**File:** `sklearn/utils/validation.py`\n\n**Key Function:** `check_array()` at lines 725-1100\n\nThe validation flow for pandas DataFrames with nullable integers:\n\n1. **Detection of pandas extension dtypes** (lines 878-896):\n```python\ndtypes_orig = list(array.dtypes)\npandas_requires_conversion = any(\n    _pandas_dtype_needs_early_conversion(i) for i in dtypes_orig\n)\n```\n\n2. **`_pandas_dtype_needs_early_conversion()`** at lines 681-717:\n```python\ndef _pandas_dtype_needs_early_conversion(pd_dtype):\n    \"\"\"Return True if pandas extension pd_dtype need to be converted early.\"\"\"\n    # ...\n    elif is_integer_dtype(pd_dtype):\n        # XXX: Warn when converting from a high integer to a float\n        return True\n```\n\nThis function correctly identifies nullable integers as needing early conversion.\n\n3. **Early conversion** (lines 935-942):\n```python\nif pandas_requires_conversion:\n    # pandas dataframe requires conversion earlier to handle extension dtypes with nans\n    new_dtype = dtype_orig if dtype is None else dtype\n    array = array.astype(new_dtype)\n    dtype = None\n```\n\n**ROOT CAUSE LOCATION #1:** `sklearn/utils/validation.py:939-940`\n\nThe issue is that when `dtype_orig` is `None` (which happens for extension dtypes that aren't standard NumPy dtypes, as seen at lines 909-913), the conversion may fail or produce unexpected results.\n\n### 3. Pandas Nullable Integer to NumPy Array Conversion\n\n**File:** `/ccb_crossrepo/src/pandas/pandas/core/arrays/masked.py`\n\n**Key Method:** `__array__()` at lines 694-716:\n\n```python\ndef __array__(\n    self, dtype: NpDtype | None = None, copy: bool | None = None\n) -> np.ndarray:\n    \"\"\"the array interface, return my values\"\"\"\n    # ...\n    return self.to_numpy(dtype=dtype, copy=copy)\n```\n\n**Key Method:** `to_numpy()` at lines 512-606:\n\n```python\ndef to_numpy(\n    self,\n    dtype: npt.DTypeLike | None = None,\n    copy: bool = False,\n    na_value: object = lib.no_default,\n) -> np.ndarray:\n    hasna = self._hasna\n    dtype, na_value = to_numpy_dtype_inference(self, dtype, na_value, hasna)\n    # ...\n```\n\n**ROOT CAUSE LOCATION #2:** `/ccb_crossrepo/src/pandas/pandas/core/arrays/_utils.py:27-75`\n\nThe `to_numpy_dtype_inference()` function determines the output dtype:\n\n```python\ndef to_numpy_dtype_inference(\n    arr: ExtensionArray,\n    dtype: npt.DTypeLike | None,\n    na_value,\n    hasna: bool,\n) -> tuple[np.dtype | None, Any]:\n    # ...\n    if dtype is None and is_numeric_dtype(arr.dtype):\n        inferred_numeric_dtype = True\n        if hasna:\n            if arr.dtype.kind == \"b\":\n                result_dtype = np.dtype(np.object_)\n            else:\n                if arr.dtype.kind in \"iu\":\n                    result_dtype = np.dtype(np.float64)  # <-- Nullable int -> float64\n                # ...\n```\n\n**Critical Finding:** When a nullable integer array contains NA values, pandas automatically converts to `float64` and replaces NA with `np.nan`. However, when there are **no** NA values:\n\n```python\nelse:\n    result_dtype = arr.dtype.numpy_dtype  # <-- Stays as integer\n```\n\n### 4. NumPy dtype Handling\n\n**File:** `/ccb_crossrepo/src/numpy/numpy/_core/_methods.py`\n\nWhen computing variance for `StandardScaler`, NumPy's `_var()` function (lines 148-215) and `_mean()` function (lines 115-146) are used:\n\n```python\ndef _mean(a, axis=None, dtype=None, out=None, keepdims=False, *, where=True):\n    arr = asanyarray(a)\n    # Cast bool, unsigned int, and int to float64 by default\n    if dtype is None:\n        if issubclass(arr.dtype.type, (nt.integer, nt.bool)):\n            dtype = mu.dtype('f8')  # Convert to float64\n```\n\n**ROOT CAUSE LOCATION #3:** `/ccb_crossrepo/src/numpy/numpy/_core/_methods.py:125-127`\n\nThe issue emerges when:\n1. A nullable integer array **without NA values** passes through pandas conversion\n2. The array stays as integer type\n3. scikit-learn's validation expects a float dtype\n4. NumPy's mean/var functions handle this internally, but the dtype mismatch can cause issues in intermediate computations\n\n## The Root Cause\n\n**Primary Root Cause:** `sklearn/utils/validation.py:894-896, 909-913, 935-940`\n\nThe root cause is in scikit-learn's `check_array()` function, specifically in how it handles the `dtype_orig` variable for pandas extension array dtypes:\n\n```python\n# Line 909-913\nelif (_is_extension_array_dtype(array) or hasattr(array, \"iloc\")) and hasattr(\n    array, \"dtype\"\n):\n    # array is a pandas series\n    # ...\n    if isinstance(array.dtype, np.dtype):\n        dtype_orig = array.dtype\n    else:\n        # Set to None to let array.astype work out the best dtype\n        dtype_orig = None  # <-- This is problematic for extension dtypes\n```\n\nWhen `dtype_orig` is `None` and `pandas_requires_conversion` is `True`, the conversion at line 939-940 uses `None` as the target dtype:\n\n```python\nnew_dtype = dtype_orig if dtype is None else dtype  # new_dtype could be None\narray = array.astype(new_dtype)  # astype(None) behavior is unpredictable\n```\n\n**Line Range of Root Cause:** `sklearn/utils/validation.py:909-942`\n\n## Secondary Contributing Factors\n\n1. **Pandas `to_numpy_dtype_inference()`**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/pandas/pandas/core/arrays/_utils.py:35-52`\n   - The inference logic differs based on whether NA values are present\n   - This creates inconsistent behavior between nullable integer arrays with and without NA values\n\n2. **NumPy mean/var dtype handling**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/numpy/numpy/_core/_methods.py:125-130, 158-160`\n   - NumPy internally converts integers to float64 for mean/variance computation\n   - However, this happens late in the pipeline, after scikit-learn's validation\n\n## Impact\n\n1. **Inconsistent Results:** Nullable integer arrays with NA values convert to `float64` with `np.nan`, while those without NA may stay as integers or convert differently\n2. **Potential Errors:** When `dtype_orig` is `None` and the requested dtype is also `None`, the resulting array dtype is unpredictable\n3. **Silent Data Corruption:** Integer values may be silently converted to floats with potential precision loss for very large integers\n\n## Recommended Fix\n\nThe fix should be in `sklearn/utils/validation.py` around lines 909-942:\n\n```python\n# Suggested fix: Explicitly handle extension dtypes\nelif (_is_extension_array_dtype(array) or hasattr(array, \"iloc\")) and hasattr(\n    array, \"dtype\"\n):\n    # array is a pandas series\n    type_if_series = type(array)\n    pandas_requires_conversion = _pandas_dtype_needs_early_conversion(array.dtype)\n    if isinstance(array.dtype, np.dtype):\n        dtype_orig = array.dtype\n    elif hasattr(array.dtype, 'numpy_dtype'):\n        # For extension dtypes that have a numpy equivalent\n        dtype_orig = array.dtype.numpy_dtype\n    else:\n        # Set to a safe default for numeric extension types\n        dtype_orig = np.float64 if pandas_requires_conversion else None\n```\n\n## Summary Table\n\n| Component | File | Line Range | Issue |\n|-----------|------|------------|-------|\n| **scikit-learn validation** | `sklearn/utils/validation.py` | 909-942 | `dtype_orig` set to `None` for extension dtypes, causing unpredictable conversion |\n| **pandas dtype inference** | `pandas/core/arrays/_utils.py` | 35-52 | Different behavior for arrays with/without NA values |\n| **pandas to_numpy** | `pandas/core/arrays/masked.py` | 512-606 | Conversion depends on NA presence |\n| **NumPy mean/var** | `numpy/_core/_methods.py` | 125-130, 158-160 | Internal int->float conversion happens after sklearn validation |\n",

A nullable integer array **without NA values** passes through pandas conversion\n2. The array stays as integer type\n3. scikit-learn's validation expects a float dtype\n4. NumPy's mean/var functions handle this internally, but the dtype mismatch can cause issues in intermediate computations\n\n## The Root Cause\n\n**Primary Root Cause:** `sklearn/utils/validation.py:894-896, 909-913, 935-940`\n\nThe root cause is in scikit-learn's `check_array()` function, specifically in how it handles the `dtype_orig` variable for pandas extension array dtypes:\n\n```python\n# Line 909-913\nelif (_is_extension_array_dtype(array) or hasattr(array, \"iloc\")) and hasattr(\n    array, \"dtype\"\n):\n    # <-- This is problematic for extension dtypes\n```\n\nWhen `dtype_orig` is `None` and `pandas_requires_conversion` is `True`, the conversion at line 939-940 uses `None` as the target dtype:\n\n```python\nnew_dtype = dtype_orig if dtype is None else dtype  # new_dtype could be None\narray = array.astype(new_dtype)  # astype(None) behavior is unpredictable\n```\n\n**Line Range of Root Cause:** `sklearn/utils/validation.py:909-942`\n\n## Secondary Contributing Factors\n\n1. **Pandas `to_numpy_dtype_inference()`**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/pandas/pandas/core/arrays/_utils.py:35-52`\n   - The inference logic differs based on whether NA values are present\n   - This creates inconsistent behavior between nullable integer arrays with and without NA values\n\n2. **NumPy mean/var dtype handling**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/numpy/numpy/_core/_methods.py:125-130, 158-160`\n   - NumPy internally converts integers to float64 for mean/variance computation\n   - However, this happens late in the pipeline, after scikit-learn's validation\n\n## Impact\n\n1. **Inconsistent Results:** Nullable integer arrays with NA values convert to `float64` with `np.nan`, while those without NA may stay as integers or convert differently\n2. **Potential Errors:** When `dtype_orig` is `None` and the requested dtype is also `None`, the resulting array dtype is unpredictable\n3. **Silent Data Corruption:** Integer values may be silently converted to floats with potential precision loss for very large integers\n\n## Recommended Fix\n\nThe fix should be in `sklearn/utils/validation.py` around lines 909-942:\n\n```python\n# Suggested fix: Explicitly handle extension dtypes\nelif (_is_extension_array_dtype(array) or hasattr(array, \"iloc\")) and hasattr(\n    array, \"dtype\"\n):\n    # For extension dtypes that have a numpy equivalent\n        dtype_orig = array.dtype.numpy_dtype\n    else:\n        # Set to a safe default for numeric extension types\n        dtype_orig = np.float64 if pandas_requires_conversion else None\n```\n\n## Summary Table\n\n| Component | File | Line Range | Issue |\n|-----------|------|------------|-------|\n| **scikit-learn validation** | `sklearn/utils/validation.py` | 909-942 | `dtype_orig` set to `None` for extension dtypes, causing unpredictable conversion |\n| **pandas dtype inference** | `pandas/core/arrays/_utils.py` | 35-52 | Different behavior for arrays with/without NA values |\n| **pandas to_numpy** | `pandas/core/arrays/masked.py` | 512-606 | Conversion depends on NA presence |\n| **NumPy mean/var** | `numpy/_core/_methods.py` | 125-130, 158-160 | Internal int->float conversion happens after sklearn validation |\n",

# NumPy dtype Compatibility Issue with Pandas Nullable Integers in scikit-learn Preprocessing

## Executive Summary

When a pandas DataFrame with nullable integer types (e.g., `pd.Int64Dtype`) is passed to scikit-learn's `StandardScaler` or `MinMaxScaler`, the conversion to NumPy arrays can fail or produce unexpected results. This analysis traces the data flow across three libraries (scikit-learn, pandas, NumPy) to identify the root cause.

## Data Flow Analysis

### 1. scikit-learn Preprocessing Input Data Flow

**Entry Point:** `sklearn/preprocessing/_data.py:961-968`

When `StandardScaler.fit()` or `partial_fit()` is called, the input is validated through `validate_data()`:

```python
X = validate_data(
    self,
    X,
    accept_sparse=("csr", "csc"),
    dtype=supported_float_dtypes(xp, X_device),
    ensure_all_finite="allow-nan",
    reset=first_call,
)
```

The `dtype=supported_float_dtypes(xp, X_device)` parameter requests conversion to floating-point types.

### 2. Input Validation in scikit-learn

**File:** `sklearn/utils/validation.py`

**Key Function:** `check_array()` at lines 725-1100

The validation flow for pandas DataFrames with nullable integers:

1. **Detection of pandas extension dtypes** (lines 878-896):
```python
dtypes_orig = list(array.dtypes)
pandas_requires_conversion = any(
    _pandas_dtype_needs_early_conversion(i) for i in dtypes_orig
)
```

2. **`_pandas_dtype_needs_early_conversion()`** at lines 681-717:
```python
def _pandas_dtype_needs_early_conversion(pd_dtype):
    """Return True if pandas extension pd_dtype need to be converted early."""
    # ...
    elif is_integer_dtype(pd_dtype):
        # XXX: Warn when converting from a high integer to a float
        return True
```
